Jiangsu Province Abolishes Sutra Chanting Tax in Various Counties

The Jiangsu Provincial Government previously ordered the suspension of the Sutra Chanting Tax at the request of the Buddhist Association. The Provincial Committee decided to instruct the Finance and Education Departments to prepare a compensation plan before complying. Subsequently, the Buddhist Association submitted a request to suspend the collection of the Sutra Chanting Tax. If the compensation is awaited, it will be difficult to wait. The Provincial Government instructed the Finance and Education Departments to report the case together. The Finance and Education Departments then submitted a report to the Provincial Government, stating that the education fees in various counties of Jiangsu Province are mostly insufficient, and some have organized Sutra Chanting donations to provide assistance. If the collection is suddenly suspended, it will undoubtedly affect education. It is necessary to comply with the order to prepare compensation to maintain education. However, since the situation in each county is different, the compensation method is difficult to standardize. It is now proposed to instruct all counties that have already organized Sutra Chanting donations to immediately convene the Finance and Education Bureaus to properly discuss the compensation method and submit it for review and transfer. Those who have not collected it will not be allowed to organize it again. This method of handling will not conflict with the orders of the Ministry and will also maintain education funding. After receiving the report, the Provincial Government submitted it to yesterday's 332nd meeting for approval in accordance with the case and has already notified the Ministry of Interior.

Yan Xishan Returns to Shijiazhuang from the Front

Jin Army Prepares to Retreat and Preserve Strength

Tianjin Dispatch: Yan Xishan took a special train from Beiping to Tianjin on the morning of the 11th to inspect the Jinpu Railway, as detailed in the previous letter. It is now learned that Yan was chased by airplanes in the middle of the journey. After arriving in Dezhou at 1:30 PM, he transferred to a car and stayed temporarily in a small village. Zhang Yinwu, Wang Jingguo, and others rushed from the front to report that the defense was solid and asked Yan not to advance. Yan insisted on seeing the front line, so he took a car to the areas of Pingyuan, Huangheya, and Yucheng on the 12th. However, it was better not to look than to look. Since the defeat in Jinan, it has been almost a month, and the morale has been declining and the military discipline has been lax, without any rectification. Yan saw this weakness and said to Zhang Yinwu, Wang Jingguo, and others, "Defend if you can, retreat if you can't." On the morning of the 13th, he took a special train back to the north from Dezhou at 4:00 AM. At 8:05 AM, he passed Cangzhou and originally planned to transfer to a car to Shijiazhuang. However, the Cangshi Highway was washed away by mountain water. At 10:00 AM, he passed Chen Guancun, and at 11:00 AM, he arrived at the Tianjin Railway Station, which was even more heavily guarded than when he passed Tianjin on the 11th. At that time, it was the third train on the Beining Railway entering the station, and passengers changed from the underground passage to enter and exit. Yan's car was parked on the third track fork. Yuan Qingzeng, Cui Tingxian, Zeng Yanjie, and others boarded the car to pay their respects and talked for a long time. At 11:40 AM, Yuan and Zeng got off the car, and Yan left Cui Tingxian alone in another private room for a secret talk. At 11:55 AM, Cui finally got off the car. Liu Encheng, director of the Jinpu Bureau, also got off the car because his escort responsibility had been completed. Yan's special train had a total of twenty cars and no first- or second-class cars. A Jinpu Blue Steel third-class dining car was more prominent. Yan was sitting in the Pinghan Railway's 301st third-class sleeper car, which was equipped with a wireless telegraph machine. The rest were all iron-covered cars and dilapidated cars. At 12:05 AM, he left Tianjin, at 0:45 AM, he passed Yangcun, at 2:40 AM, he passed Anding, at 3:00 AM, he passed Huangcun, and at 3:30 AM, he passed Fengtai and transferred to the Pinghan Railway to Shijiazhuang. He will not return to Taiyuan and will go south to meet Feng Yuxiang to discuss new plans. Tianjin Mayor Cui Tingxian told reporters that the defeat on the Jinpu Railway was due to the failure of the Security Division. The so-called "pulling one hair moves the whole body." Jinan could not be defended, and the left and right wings had to retreat. It was rumored that Zhuan Zuoyi was responsible for the front, and because the pursuing troops were too urgent, he set fire to the Yellow River Railway Bridge. At that time, the Yellow River was flooded, and the railway bridge was burned. The retreating troops on the left and right wings were unable to retreat because there were too few ferries, and more than 30,000 people were captured. It is said that the loss of rifles was more than 2,000 machine guns, more than 300 mortars, more than 30 cannons, more than 500 cars, and more than 1,500 freight cars. Cui's words are indeed the real situation. The 16th Army stationed in the Tangshan, Kaiping, and Luanzhou areas was ordered to withdraw to Shijiazhuang, and a part of it has been mobilized. On the 12th, the army commander Yang Chengyuan rushed to Dezhou to ask Yan which army to fill the defense. Yan said, "You only need to withdraw, you don't need to ask which army will fill the defense." Yan's words are most noteworthy. Xie Lian, commander of the Jinpu Railway督战 (supervisory warfare) , led eight supervisory warfare teams from Yucheng by special train to the north on the morning of the 13th and passed Tianjin at 9:00 PM to Shijiazhuang. Based on these two points, it can be proved that there is no war to supervise on the Jinpu Railway, and preparations are being made to defend Jin Province as a base.

Recently, the local newspapers have gradually revealed the matter of the Northeast sending troops. The military authorities have not interfered. It is said that the Northeast sent troops to fill the defense of the Beining Railway due to the withdrawal of the 16th Army of the Jin faction. The Northeast's highest-ranking cadre conference has not yet been officially held because Tang Yulin, chairman of Rehe, has not arrived. Wan Fulin, Zhang Zuoxiang, Zhang Jinghui, Zou Zuohua, Zang Shiyi, Yu Xuezhong, and others who have arrived in Shenyang have exchanged opinions several times. In general, they all hope for peace in the current situation and oppose formally sending troops to participate in any aspect. At present, the opinions of representatives from all aspects in Shenyang are also very inconsistent. Both the north and the south hope that Zhang Xueliang will come out and say something fair so that the war can be resolved as soon as possible. Although Zhang has this intention, he has no such power, so armed mediation is absolutely impossible. If peaceful political methods are used to mediate, both public friendship with the south and private relations with the north must be taken into account, and a way must be found to start. This is an important issue worthy of research in the Northeast's highest-ranking cadre conference. Sun Chuanfang believes that it is more powerful for the Northeast to speak out after the two sides have fought several more battles and one side has reached a state of military exhaustion and financial exhaustion. This statement is also valued by senior Northeast generals and will be submitted to the formal meeting on the 15th for discussion. In addition to the rumors that Zhang Xueliang has ordered Zang Shiyi, Zou Zuohua, Yu Xuezhong, Ji Yiqiao, and other four divisions to prepare to enter the customs, reporters have inquired about all aspects and no one denies it. There are even those who say that the Northeast has internally decided that Zang Shiyi will be the chairman of the Hebei Provincial Government, Zou Zuohua will be the commander of the Pingjin Garrison, Yu Xuezhong will be the commander of the Tianjin Garrison, and Ji Yiqiao will be the commander of the Beiping Garrison. These are all speculations and are too far from the facts.

Page 8

According to a person from the military agency, Yan Xishan knew that although Jinan had fallen, he did not know that the Jin army had failed to an irreparable point. On the 7th of this month, Yan went north from Shijiazhuang and wanted to see the Jinpu area. Zhang Yinwu heard the news and took a special train to Changxindian to dissuade him, falsely claiming that the front-line defense was solid and the morale was strong, and that enemy planes were coming to drop bombs from time to time. The總座 (general leader) did not need to risk going there. After Yan arrived in Beiping and took the chair, he was still not at ease with the military affairs in front, so he decided to go and see. After inspecting, he realized that the military future was hopeless, so he sternly ordered Zhang Yinwu and others to defend for three weeks and wait for instructions. There is still a glimmer of hope, which is to ask Feng Yuxiang to be solely responsible for the Pinghan and Longhai railways and to ask the Northeast Army to take over the defense of Hebei Province. If the Northeast Army does not come to take over the defense, then ask Zhang Xueliang to stand in the position of the people and advise Feng and Yan to step down and go abroad, and leave the national affairs to the people. Yan has arrived in Shijiazhuang and is about to go south to discuss this matter with Feng between Xinxiang and Zhangde. If Feng agrees, Yan will return to Ping and send another responsible representative out of the customs to explain to Zhang that Yan is willing to step down and go abroad and ask Zhang to come out to mediate. In short, within a month, the situation and military affairs will undergo a new transformation and open a new act. (September 14)

Wuhu Express

The Ministry of Finance issued short-term customs treasury bills, and Anhui Province was assigned to raise 1.5 million yuan. The Provincial Government has assigned the Wuhu City to raise 60,000 yuan and Wuhu County to raise 22,000 yuan, to be paid in two installments by mid-September and the end of September.

Recently, the small steamers from Wuhu to the inland have been repeatedly robbed. The Datong and Hefei routes have been robbed many times, causing huge losses. The General Chamber of Commerce has requested the Garrison Regiment to send troops to protect them based on the requests of various merchants. The regiment has sent troops to escort the steamers from today, and all small steamers in various places have resumed operations.

The Provincial Government previously discussed abolishing the Wuhu Municipal Preparatory Office, but this has been temporarily shelved and submitted to the Central Government for resolution. Therefore, the office is now working as usual. It is now scheduled to begin dismantling the North Gate tower and city walls tomorrow, and the Municipal Public Security Bureau has been notified to send police to take care of it. (17th)

Local Correspondence

Songjiang

Suppression Commander Convenes Meeting: The four counties of Songjiang, Qingpu, Jinshan, and Pinghu, which border Jiangsu and Zhejiang, have been repeatedly harassed by bandits, causing great harm. Looting, arson, and murder are too terrible to witness. The military and police are tired of running around to suppress them, making it difficult to start. Local residents have flocked to the cities and towns, and the commercial activity in the countryside has plummeted. It is learned that Xiong Shihui, the Commander-in-Chief of Bandit Suppression for the three provinces, has specially appointed Hu Zhengji as the Bandit Suppression Commander for the four counties, responsible for supervising and suppressing them within a time limit. Yesterday, Commander Hu convened a bandit suppression meeting in Zhujing, with the county magistrates and public security bureau chiefs of the four counties, Chen Zekuan, district chief of the Jiangsu Water Police District, Xu Pucheng, district chief of the Zhejiang Water Police District, and others. Commander Hu presided over the meeting, and the county magistrate of this county, Jin, and the water police captain Fan Zicheng, and others personally attended. Each reported on the situation of bandit harassment in their jurisdiction, and then decided on the bandit suppression implementation methods before adjourning. It is heard that Pinghu County will propose that representatives from all walks of life in the four counties be jointly elected to form an organization to prepare for the commander's consultation on bandit suppression matters in order to avoid isolation. Personnel are currently being sent to various counties to solicit opinions so that they can be implemented as soon as possible.

Court Leaders Scheduled to Take Oath: The County Court of this county has been established for more than a month, but the oath ceremony has not yet been held. The court has scheduled it to be held on the 20th, and invitations have been sent to various groups to attend the ceremony.

Suzhou

Appeal Judgment of Qiantai Cheng Robbery: Two robbers, Wei Zhihe and Guo Desheng, who were involved in the Qiantai Cheng robbery case outside Xumen, appealed to the High Court against the judgment of the local court. The High Court opened a hearing on the case the day before yesterday. Wei withdrew his appeal in court. As for 墎 Desheng, he was sentenced to five years and six months of imprisonment by Judge Zheng of the Second Criminal Court yesterday (18th). A large group of bandit ships fled to Yishan Lake. Yesterday morning (18th) at 4:00 AM, a large group of more than thirty bandit ships fled from Yangcheng Lake through the Wusong River estuary to Yishan Lake. In addition to dispatching the 2nd police unit stationed there to pursue and suppress them, a telegram was sent to the county government, and the Public Security Bureau also received a call from Nie Ziyang, director of the Chefang Twelfth Branch, stating that many bandit ships arrived at the Chefang Dayao Chenghu Lake on the afternoon of the 17th. There were sixteen ships with small red flags at the bow, twenty ships with green flags, and eighteen ships with white flags. At about 3:00 PM, they began to move. At 4:00 PM, the twenty ships with green flags sailed towards the Wusong River, the sixteen ships with red flags sailed towards the Jiaolu Guanyintang area, and the eighteen ships with white flags sailed towards the West Caosi of Wujiang. Afterwards, one gang of green flags went down the Dayao Dang Baping to the Wusong River, and did not rob along the way. After arriving at Guanpu at night, they turned towards Wujiang. In addition, when these three kinds of bandit ships were sailing, the front team each had three or four small ships in advance, and several bandits in gray military uniforms stood at the bow of the ship holding guns. This morning (18th) at 11:00 AM, another 300 refugees from Hunan arrived in Chefang Town, taking 20 ships and sending representatives to the Public Security Bureau to request relief and lodging. It was decided that they would go to Wujiang today (19th) and they were escorted by the branch to the Dayimiao Temple in the city for rest.

川沙

Investigation into the Confiscated Reactionary Publications: The District Party Rectification Committee confiscated two copies of "Modern Youth" at the post office on the morning of the 14th. These were sent from Shanghai to Chen Huifang and Chen Qiyuan, students of the private Yiguang Girls' School outside the East Gate. After examining the contents of the books, they were deemed to be propaganda materials from reactionary elements, and were immediately confiscated. Chen and others were suspected of being reactionary and reported to the county government.

After receiving the approval from the county government, police were dispatched to the school that afternoon to search for other reactionary publications. Subsequently, one copy each of "Modern Youth" and "Pudong Youth" were seized. The two female students were then taken to the county government. After questioning by County Magistrate Ruan, it was learned that Chen Huifang was sixteen years old and from Shanghai, while Chen Qiyuan was thirteen years old and from Hengsha in this county. Both "Modern Youth" and "Pudong Youth" were sent by Shen Keqin, who is currently a teacher at the private Chen's Elementary School in Lannidu. After obtaining the confession, County Magistrate Ruan immediately prepared a document and dispatched police to Lannidu to arrest Shen Keqin. According to him, he had a teacher-student relationship with the two female students. The confiscated publications had been reviewed and registered by the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters and the Bureau of Education, and contained no reactionary text. County Magistrate Ruan, considering the case concerned reactionaries and that the county had no authority to handle it, ordered the court police to detain the two female students surnamed Chen in the county government, and placed the suspect Shen Keqin under the custody of the Public Security Bureau, pending the preparation of a document to be sent to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters for review.

Investigation into the Accusations Against the County Magistrate: Ruan Kaiji, the county magistrate of this county, was accused of ten counts of offenses by the District Party Affairs Rectification Committee, which was presented to the province requesting his removal from office. It is now learned that the provincial government, after receiving the report, appointed Kong Chong, the county magistrate of Nanhui, to investigate thoroughly. Kong arrived in Chuansha on the afternoon of the 16th to conduct the investigation with great secrecy. On the morning of the 17th, he met with County Magistrate Ruan at the county government, inquiring about everything, and then took a boat back to Nanhui.

Villagers Gathering to Gamble, Resisting Arrest, and Beating Police: Recently, gambling dens have opened in the tea shops of Beiqifang in Qingcheng City. Upon receiving a report, the county government telegraphed the chief of the 15th Public Security Sub-bureau to investigate and arrest the gamblers. The bureau chief, upon receiving the order, immediately led the police to make arrests. They caught gamblers such as Zhang Hemo, Tang A'er, Hua Renjin, and Yin A'du, along with gambling paraphernalia such as pots, bowls, and mahjong tiles. Just as they were about to be taken to the bureau, the owners and gamblers shouted loudly to attack, and hundreds of ignorant villagers gathered to snatch away the arrested gamblers and gambling equipment, injuring policemen Qian Guangrong and Zheng Guangming. One pistol was lost. Restaurant Industry Opposes Banquet Tax: The County Bureau of Education plans to implement a banquet tax to allocate funds for education. The measures have been drafted and submitted to the provincial government for approval. The restaurant industry has resolutely opposed this and petitioned the provincial government. The provincial government rejected the petition. The Bureau of Education is determined to collect the tax and is currently rushing to complete the collection procedures. However, Wang Juting, the representative of the restaurant industry, is unwilling to accept the decision of the provincial government and has filed another appeal with the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce of the National Government, and has also submitted a request to the county government for review.

Two Boats Collide, One Person Drowns: Wang Wenfa, a boatman from Jiangbei, was sailing a freighter from the Yu Kang Silkworm Moth Factory yesterday afternoon around 1 PM, heading towards the Silkworm Moth Farm. While passing the Liangxi River Xihu Steamboat Wharf outside Guangfu Gate and next to the Gongyun Bridge, a rice boat came head-on. Wang Wenfa was unable to avoid it and was violently hit by the rice boat. Wang Wenfa lost his footing and fell into the river. By the time he was rescued, he had already drowned. The rice boat boatman, seeing that he had caused the accident, abandoned the boat and fled without a trace. The head of the ward, together with Wang Lu, the wife of the deceased, reported the incident to the county for examination. It was determined that the deceased had been knocked into the river and died. After the examination, the corpse was ordered to be placed in a coffin for burial by the family, and the police were dispatched to detain the rice boat pending the arrest of the criminal and the administration of justice.

Eight guns and ammunition were confiscated. They went to other places to search for bandits, but the bandits all fled. Wu A'zhao was shot dead on the spot as a warning. However, Dai Kechang was released because he showed some kind of symbol specially issued by Taibao A'shu.

In addition, many people in the area have recently received threatening letters, such as the home of Dr. Lü Mengbo in Ruheziwei (who had been blackmailed once before), the home of farmer Gong Yousheng in Tingziqiao (who had been robbed and blackmailed twice before), the home of Lu Youqiao in Baijingqiao, and the home of farmer Yao A'jin, etc.

湖州

Police and Bandits in a Decisive Battle at Heshangqiao: Zhang Qiaoli, the chief of the Daixi Township Public Security Sub-bureau in Huzhou, received a confidential report the day before yesterday stating that a group of bandits had gathered in the Heshangqiao area near the town and were hiding many kidnapped victims. The crepe industry expressed its determination to crack down on the matter because it concerns the livelihood and future of the industry. Bandits Rob Zhou Furong's Home: The home of Zhou Furong, a farmer in Zibaian, about three miles from Xincang, was suddenly attacked by more than ten bandits armed with wooden sticks and iron rulers, with powdered faces and local accents, late at night on the 14th. Education News

Important News

Ministry of Education

Circular Restricting Elementary School Song and Dance Performances

The Ministry of Education has issued a circular to the education bureaus of all provinces and cities to restrict elementary school song and dance performances:

Recently, it has been found that elementary schools in various places often have song and dance performances. Preparations take a long time in advance, and teaching time almost occupies a large part of music and sports time. The time taken by a scene or a song at the event also takes up dozens of minutes. Children often sing and dance until they are sweating, gasping for breath, and hoarse. The purpose of this is to entertain guests at meetings and parent-teacher conferences, but there are also cases where private celebrations are held to gather entertainment for entertainment. According to the temporary standards for the elementary school curriculum issued by the Ministry, physical education and dance are limited to folk dances, etc., and music stipulates that simplified notation should not be used unless absolutely necessary. The dance in the song and dance drama is different from folk dances, etc., and teaching music with simplified notation is also inconsistent with the standard regulations. Moreover, singing and dancing use both sound and strength, and the time is long, which is more detrimental to children's physical education. As for using children as entertainment items to win personal favor, it is even more incompatible with the purpose of education. In short, this kind of song and dance drama has more harm than good, and should be restricted in a unified manner. Each school should not hold such performances more than twice a year. The materials taken should not be too long, and no long-term preparations should be made in advance, and no long-term performances should be made at the event. In addition to issuing separate orders, this order is hereby issued to the Ministry to pay close attention to and instruct its subordinates to comply with this order.

Hunan Education Director Wei Protects Education

Changsha was previously captured by the communist bandits, and all material construction was destroyed, and the loss of education was the greatest. Hunan Chairman He Yun has decided to allocate funds to open schools. However, the province's education fund and salt tax surcharge for education were borrowed due to the emergency of the communist suppression military affairs. Therefore, the funding is quite difficult. Huang Shiwei, the current director of the Hunan Education Bureau, is temporarily staying in Shanghai and has sent a letter to the Hunan Chairman, insisting that education funds cannot be used for other purposes, and those that have been borrowed must be returned by the Ministry of Finance so that schools can open on time. Otherwise, he will only resign to apologize to the education community. Here is a copy of the letter from Huang to He Yunqiao:

Chairman Yun Gong's seat, respectfully and solemnly, I returned to the province from Chenzhou a month ago and suffered from summer dampness. My mother was trapped in a dangerous city and suffered from the burning, killing, and terror, which caused fright. I had to come to Shanghai for medical treatment. I had to entrust Director Yu Ke to act on my behalf. Being away from the province for ten days, the affairs of Hunan are in an emergency. I am a member of the provincial committee and cannot follow you to share your worries. I feel extremely guilty. I have received letters from the education community stating that the government has borrowed the education fund stored in the bank, and has not received the monthly salt tax surcharge of tens of thousands of yuan. Education in Hunan will be suspended. If so, the hard-working teachers will lose their jobs, and the ambitious youth will lose their schooling. I think that to appease people's hearts, it is necessary to actively prepare for the opening of schools to make up for the deficiencies. When I left Hunan, I entrusted Director Zhang and Director Yu Ke to present it to you. Later, I received a letter from the Education Bureau informing me that our government accepted my opinion and decided to open schools on October 1. I am very happy with this approach. However, the fund has been withdrawn, the salt surcharge has not been resolved, and there is still no funding. It is still difficult to determine when the schools will open. I sincerely hope that you will maintain your enthusiasm for protecting education from beginning to end, and order the Ministry of Finance to return the borrowed education funds to the bank in installments, so as to avoid the name of borrowing educational funds. At the same time, please negotiate with Special Envoy Li to allocate the old amount of eight jiao per bag of salt tax surcharge to the management committee for responsible custody and distribution. On one hand, order the Ministry of Finance to issue funds as soon as possible to prepare for the opening of schools, and check the established cases and subsidize the insufficient expenses on a monthly basis so that education will not be interrupted. In this way, the war will be quelled and the music will not stop. This is also what you would like to do. Otherwise, empty promises will be difficult to fulfill. After thinking about it, I have no choice but to resign and retreat to make way for the capable. I humbly ask for your attention and instructions. I respectfully wish you peace and prosperity. I am very grateful. Huang Shiheng bows to you on September 16.

Order Issued by the Department of Education

Measures for the Handover of Provincial Educational Institutions

Temporary Measures for Handover of Educational Institutions in Jiangsu Province

Chapter 1: General Provisions

Article 1: These measures shall apply to all levels of provincial schools, social education institutions, county education bureaus, and county educational institutions.

Article 2: Principal officers of educational institutions who have served for more than one month, whether in a permanent or acting capacity, shall handle handover procedures in accordance with these measures.

Article 3: Departing officers and personnel bearing joint responsibility, as mentioned in the preceding article, shall not leave their posts without proper settlement and reporting.

Article 4: In the event of resignation due to illness, dismissal, or death in office, the handover shall be carried out by the personnel jointly responsible.

Article 5: When handover procedures are carried out by provincial educational institutions and county education bureaus, the Department of Education may, if necessary, appoint an auditor to supervise the joint accounting. The county magistrate shall serve as the supervisor of the county education bureau's handover. For county educational institutions, the auditor may be appointed by the county education bureau.

Article 6: For those who have served less than one month, the handover from the previous officer may be directly transferred to the succeeding officer for continued handling. However, a detailed statement of all income and expenditure during the current term shall still be submitted to the succeeding officer for review and joint accounting.

Chapter 2: Handover

Article 7: Departing officers shall prepare a list of the following items under their management and hand them over to the succeeding officer:

1. Amount of various revenues.

2. Amount of actual expenditures and remaining funds.

3. Deeds for educational properties and other items under management.

4. Various ledgers, registers, vouchers, and files. However, those related to financial transactions and documents requiring continued processing shall be transferred as special cases.

5. Stubs of receipts for collected donations and rentals, and unused receipts.

6. Goods and equipment.

Article 8: Any remaining funds handled by the departing officer shall be handed over to the succeeding officer for safekeeping within five days after the handover.

Article 9: Any expenditures not yet reported or reports not yet paid for by the departing officer shall be itemized according to the budget items, with the actual amounts listed and handed over to the succeeding officer.

Article 10: Financial handover shall be based on the expenditure approval documents and receipt stubs issued, as well as bank or money house passbooks for receipts. For expenditures, it shall be based on approved budget documents and receipts. For direct collection of donations, it shall be based on the receipt book.

Chapter 3: Audit

Article 11: Upon receiving the handover list from the previous officer, the succeeding officer shall immediately verify each item and prepare a reply list, which shall be submitted to the previous officer, auditor, and supervisor for scheduled joint accounting.

Article 12: The succeeding officer's audit shall be based on the previous officer's master and detailed lists.

Chapter 4: Joint Accounting

Article 13: The date of the joint accounting shall be determined by the succeeding officer, who shall notify the previous officer, auditor, and supervisor accordingly.

Article 14: The joint accounting shall be conducted within the respective institutions, unless special circumstances dictate otherwise.

Article 15: In the event of financial disputes between the previous and succeeding officers, the supervisor or auditor shall render an impartial judgment. If the judgment fails to resolve the dispute, the matter may be submitted to the Department of Education for review and resolution. However, for county educational institutions, it shall first be submitted to the Education Bureau for review and resolution.

Article 16: During the joint accounting handover, the financial audit committee of the respective institutions may publicly elect two members to participate.

Article 17: After the settlement of the handover accounting, the supervisor, auditor, previous and succeeding officers, and members of the audit committee shall sign and seal the handover document.

Article 18: After the joint accounting is finalized, the previous and succeeding officers shall jointly submit a report to the Department of Education for review. However, county educational institutions shall submit separate reports to the County Education Bureau and the County Government.

Chapter 5: Time Limits

Article 19: The time limit for handover of provincial educational institutions and county education bureaus shall be forty days from the date of arrival of the succeeding officer; for those who have served less than one month, the time limit shall be twenty days. The allocation of time is as follows:

(A) For those who have served more than one month:

1. Previous officer to prepare and hand over the list: 10 days.

2. Succeeding officer to audit and prepare reply list: 10 days.

3. Completion of joint accounting: 10 days.

4. Submission of report to the Department for review: 10 days.

(B) For those who have served less than one month:

1. Previous officer to prepare and hand over the statement: 4 days.

2. Succeeding officer to audit: 4 days.

3. Completion of joint accounting: 4 days.

4. Submission of report to the Department for review: 8 days.

(The handover period for county educational institutions shall not exceed twenty days.)

Chapter 6: Penalties

Article 20: If the previous officer falsifies the handover list, the succeeding officer shall report the matter jointly with the supervisor and auditor for investigation and recovery according to law.

Article 21: If the previous officer delays in preparing and handing over the list for more than one month, a strict deadline shall be set for compliance. If the matter remains unresolved after the deadline, and if any misappropriation is discovered, the relevant judicial authorities may be notified to seize the officer's private property for compensation, while still pursuing recovery.

Article 22: In the event of death in office with misappropriation, the provisions of the preceding article may be applied to the officer's estate, taking into account the circumstances.

Article 23: If the handover is overdue and the officer absconds, and if the succeeding officer discovers any misappropriation, the matter shall be handled in accordance with Article 20 and reported to the relevant judicial authorities for investigation and prosecution.

Article 24: If, after the audit is completed and the report is jointly submitted, it is discovered that the previous officer has omitted or embezzled funds, the succeeding officer shall be held responsible for compensation.

Chapter 7: Supplementary Provisions

Article 25: Matters not covered in these measures may be amended at any time.

Article 26: These measures shall take effect six days after being resolved and promulgated by the Jiangsu Provincial Government Committee. (End)

Shanghai Wusong Middle School Focuses on Student Academics

Since adding a grade last autumn, the Municipal Wusong Middle School has implemented ability grouping in the three subjects of Chinese, English, and Mathematics to accommodate students' individual characteristics and abilities, with good results. This academic year, due to educational funding issues, the added grade was cancelled, and the ability grouping system could not be continued. To remedy the uneven academic levels of students, it has been decided that teachers will gather students with weaker academic performance every evening starting at 7:00 PM for supplementary instruction. Teachers are providing this service voluntarily without additional compensation.

Municipal Yangzheng School Constructs New Building

The Municipal Yangzheng School is in dire need of rebuilding due to the tilting of the school building. Principal Li has been planning this for years, and it is now ready. The construction contract has been approved by the Municipal Government and the Education Bureau and was signed yesterday. Construction has begun on ten three-story reinforced concrete buildings with eight classrooms, one large auditorium, and two offices. The total cost is over 40,000 yuan. In addition to the school's accumulated funds of over 10,000 yuan, Principal Li has secured loans and donations of 27,000 yuan. The loans will be repaid by the school annually in the future.

Yu Binqi Initiates Table Tennis Referee Association

Since the establishment of the Table Tennis Federation in Shanghai in 1918, table tennis has become popular throughout the country. However, the rules have not been uniformly standardized. A survey of inland areas such as Zhejiang, Shaoxing, Xiaoshan, Jiangsu, Kunshan, and Taicang reveals that the rules are still similar to tennis. Senior sports figures fear that those familiar with this sport are few, resulting in a lack of qualified referees. Fortunately, in the spring of 1927, Japan sent representatives such as Kushima and Kido to Shanghai to organize international table tennis rules with Chinese representatives Lin Zecang, Hu Tiewu, Yu Binqi, Jin Jiming, He Yiyun, and foreign representatives such as Englishman Hawkins and American Egglai. The rules have been used in the Far East Games and have been well received. However, although the rules have been in effect for several years, a referee association has yet to be organized. Taking advantage of the current Champagne Cup competition, which is attracting many talented players and is fiercely competitive, Yu Binqi is organizing such an association. All table tennis enthusiasts who are keen to participate and jointly study and who wish to become referees can register in person within two days at the Racecourse Club, 323 De Fu Li, Mahuo Road. The rules will be given away for free.

Municipal Government Orders Finance Bureau to Collect Rent Surtax

Collection to Begin September 30

Publication of Detailed Rules for Rent Surtax

The Municipal Government has been ordered to raise 1 million yuan in 1929 customs revenue short-term treasury bonds. After organizing a fundraising committee, it formulated a method of exchanging the bonds by levying a two-month rent surtax. Details were reported yesterday. It is learned that the Municipal Government yesterday instructed the Municipal Finance Bureau to instruct various collection offices to begin collecting the surtax from September 30, to be collected in two installments within the stipulated two months, without delay. The Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau's detailed rules for raising 1929 customs revenue short-term treasury bonds by levying a rent surtax have been approved and published. The full text of the instruction and the detailed rules for the rent surtax are hereby reproduced as follows:

Instruction: Regarding the matter of complying with the order, the regulations for raising 1929 customs revenue short-term treasury bonds by levying a rent surtax in this city have now been submitted to the 165th Municipal Government meeting for deliberation, amendment, and approval. In addition to the announcement, the aforementioned regulations are hereby issued for your bureau to comply with and instruct the various collection offices to begin collecting the surtax from September 30, to be collected in two installments within the stipulated two months, without any delay. This is essential.

Detailed Rules: Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau's Detailed Rules for Raising 1929 Customs Revenue Short-Term Treasury Bonds by Levying a Rent Surtax

Article 1: All matters related to raising treasury bonds by levying a rent surtax in this city shall be handled in accordance with the regulations for raising 1929 customs revenue short-term treasury bonds by levying a rent surtax, as well as the provisions of these detailed rules.

Article 2: The rent surtax shall be collected by personnel from the four collection offices of the bureau (Southeast, Northwest) by segment and household.

Article 3: Each collection office shall prepare a general collection register, divided into columns for street name, neighborhood name, household name, monthly rent, and remarks, to be filled in based on the rent register for verification.

Article 4: The triplicate rent surtax receipt shall be printed by the bureau with serial numbers and stamped with the bureau's seal. It shall be distributed to the various collection offices, which shall fill in the receipts according to the items listed in the general register, submit them for verification, and keep them for file. Detailed verification shall be carried out to avoid errors.

Article 5: Collection personnel shall wear temporary badges when collecting the rent surtax for identification.

Article 6: When collection personnel receive rent, they shall immediately issue a receipt to the tenant for safekeeping.

Article 7: The funds collected by each collector each day shall be submitted along with one copy of the receipt to the collection office for verification and collection before 4:00 PM, so that they can be settled and deposited into the treasury.

Article 8: When each collection office collects the funds submitted by each collector, it shall verify the submission against the general collection register by household. The verifier shall stamp the remarks column for verification. The verification copy shall be submitted to the bureau for review.

Article 9: Each collection office shall deposit the total amount collected each day into the designated bank for special storage and report the total amount to the bureau for record.

Article 10: When collection personnel collect the rent surtax, they shall provide detailed explanations to residents who have questions and shall not act rashly.

Article 11: When collection personnel collect the rent surtax, they may be assisted by police officers from the various districts of the Public Security Bureau. In the event of resistant or uncooperative households, they may request the nearest police district to handle the matter at its discretion.

Article 12: Each collection office shall increase the number of inspectors at any time and conduct strict random checks and investigations. If collectors are found to be acting irregularly, they shall be sent to the bureau for strict punishment.

Article 13: Collection offices and collectors who perform well and achieve special results may submit a request for awards to encourage them.

Article 14: These detailed rules shall take effect from the date of approval and publication by the Municipal Government.

City Finance Discussion Committee Held Inaugural Meeting Yesterday

Wang Xiaolai Elected Chairman

Xu Jiqing and Zhu Dazhai Elected Vice-Chairmen

The Shanghai Municipal Finance Discussion Committee held its inaugural meeting and first meeting at 6:00 PM yesterday at the Bank Association, 4th floor. Details are summarized below:

Attendees: Finance Bureau Director Tang Naikang, and Xu Jiqing, Shen Lianfang, Wang Binyan, Qin Run卿, Jin Lüqin, Li Quanshi, Pan Xulun, Yao Mulian, Wang Yansong, Zhu Dazhai, Xu Yongzuo, Ye Huijun, Xu Fu, Wang Xiaolai, Yu Hongjun, Shen Tianxin, Yu Qia卿, and other eighteen people. Xu Peikun, Hu Mengjia, Qian Xinzhi, and Li Fuxun did not attend due to other commitments.

Meeting Agenda: (1) Opening; (2) Finance Bureau Director as Temporary Chairman; (3) All stand at attention and bow three times to the national flag and the portrait of the Prime Minister; (4) Read the Prime Minister's will respectfully; (5) Temporary Chairman delivers opening remarks; (6) Speeches; (7) Elect Chairman and Vice-Chairmen; (8) Hold the first meeting; (9) Adjournment; (10) Banquet.

Chairman's Remarks: Temporary Chairman Tang briefly stated that today is the inaugural meeting and first meeting of the committee, and he is grateful for the attendance of all committee members. The necessity of establishing this committee is due to the fact that the Municipal Government has a construction discussion committee, but it cannot specialize in financial matters, hence the decision to form this committee. Municipal finance has always been open. Now, the Finance Bureau, to promote openness, is publishing a quarterly to allow citizens to understand finance, which can also serve as a reference for policymakers. Naikang especially wants to thoroughly improve the system and respects everyone as economic and financial experts or local elders of Shanghai, and specially invited them to serve as committee members so that policy implementation will not be isolated and can be easily carried out. Proper financial reorganization requires collective thinking and effort. He hopes for guidance on all matters in the future. The constitution and rules of the committee have already been drafted. He requests everyone present to discuss them, elect a chairman, and hold the first meeting. He hopes everyone will express their insightful opinions. Li Quanshi, Wang Yansong, and Ye Huijun then delivered speeches successively, followed by a response from Director Tang.

Election of Chairman: After the speeches, the election of the chairman began. Wang Xiaolai was elected as the Chairman, and Xu Jiqing and Zhu Dazhai were elected as the Vice-Chairmen.

First Meeting Agenda: (1) Chairman respectfully reads the Prime Minister's will; (2) Report on matters; (3) Discussion matters; (4) Bylaws of the committee; (5) Committee members identify matters for group review and nominate group leaders.

First Meeting: The elected Chairman immediately held the first meeting. Chairman Wang Xiaolai respectfully read the will. The Chairman first reported the significance of the establishment of the assembly, stating that it had been reported by Director Tang and would not be repeated. Then, the by-laws were discussed and it was decided to submit it to the Finance and Administration Group for review. (2) Committee members identify matters for group review and nominate group leaders.

Committee Members of Each Group: It was decided that the Finance and Administration Group would have five members: Xu Fu, Shen Lianfang, Hu Mengjia, Shen Tianxin, Yu Hongjun, with Shen Lianfang as the director. (2) The Economics Group would have four members: Qin Run卿, Xu Peikun, Wang Yansong, Li Fuxun, with Qin Run卿 as the director. (3) The Tax Group would have four members: Yu Qia卿, Li Quanshi, Zhu Dazhai, Jin Lüqin, with Yu Qia卿 as the director. (4) The Accounting Group would have four members: Xu Yongzuo, Pan Xulun, Jin Lüqin, Xu Jiqing, with Xu Yongzuo as the director. (5) The Municipal Property Group would have four members: Shen Lianfang, Ye Huijun, Yao Mulian, Wang Binyan, with Yao Mulian as the director. (6) The Public Debt Group would have five members: Zhu Dazhai, Qian Xinzhi, Shen Tianxin, Li Quanshi, Wang Xiaolai, with Qian Xinzhi as the director. The meeting adjourned at approximately 8:00 PM, followed by a banquet.

Opposition to Water Rate Increase

The Public Works Department Will Reconsider

Meeting: According to the Ta Mei Wan Pao (Shanghai Evening Post & Mercury), the Public Works Department of the Public Concession held a routine board meeting yesterday (17th) afternoon, as various Chinese groups have been opposing the water rate increase. They discussed whether the resolution on this matter could be reconsidered. However, according to a senior official of the department, the discussion only concerned the possibility of submitting it for reconsideration at the next meeting, and the resolution itself was not discussed. Furthermore, today (18th), the Chairman of the Public Works Department, Fessenden, met with officials from the Water Company for a long time to discuss the water price increase issue, but the content remains confidential.

Reply: The Chief of the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession, McKnoton, replied yesterday to a letter from the Shanghai Real Estate Association, translated as follows: In response to the five points raised in your letter of September 12th, the answers are as follows: 1. The amount of the net profit loss this year depends on how the exchange rate changes, and especially on the exchange rate when dividends are paid out next March. Assuming the exchange rate is one shilling and six pence, the statutory dividends to be paid will be approximately 646,242 taels of silver. The surcharge can make up for this loss, approximately 215,000 taels of silver. 2. The reserve fund under (average dividend) is approximately 380,000 taels of silver. This reserve fund, together with the increased surcharge, will be used to make up for the aforementioned loss. It is estimated that there will still be a shortfall of 51,242 taels of silver. 3. If the exchange rate is one shilling and seven pence and a quarter when dividends are paid, then approximately 55,225 taels, 3 dimes, and 4 mils of silver can be saved on the dividend payment. 4. According to the contract stipulated in 1928, the various stocks must be paid interest annually as stipulated by law. If the net profit this year is insufficient to pay interest, it will be supplemented from the net profit of the following year. 5. The contract stipulated in 1928 states that the water price will be revised every five years after the revision on July 1, 1929. It can be revised at any time with the consent of both parties. The current rate period lasts until June 30, 1931. It has now been agreed to extend the period to the end of next year. It is proposed to request the Public Works Department to investigate the accounts of the Water Company. This article has been implemented every six months since the 1928 contract was signed. As for this price increase, the Public Works Department will reconsider it in the coming days. We will inform you of the decision in another letter. Finally, one last word: the public utilities mentioned in your letter must be owned by the city, and public interests should be prioritized, which is reasonable. However, this issue is of great concern, and the opinions of experts are difficult to reconcile. It seems that a detailed discussion cannot be made in this limited space. We hereby reply for your information.

Propaganda Department of the Shanghai Special City Party Headquarters of the Chinese Kuomintang

Again Requesting a Ban on the Import of Japanese Silkworm Cocoons

The issue of Japanese silkworm cocoons being shipped to China has already aroused the reaction of Chinese people and silk cocoon merchants across the country. Recently, the customs has ordered a ban on the import of Japanese silkworm cocoons. Yesterday, the Zhejiang General Chamber of Commerce sent a letter and telegram to the General Association of Silk Cocoons of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui provinces and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, requesting them to find ways to stop it. The original text is recorded below:

Letter to the General Association of Silk Cocoons: Respectfully, our association received a telegram from the Jiaxing Silk Cocoon Association stating that the import of Japanese dry cocoons will lead to the demise of the Chinese silk cocoon industry, which is of great importance to national taxes and commerce. The telegram requests a swift method of resistance, which is a common feeling. We believe that the import of foreign raw materials is a good sign of the progress of our country's industry, and free international trade is not something we should reject or accept. What is strange is that your association holds the key to the silk cocoons of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui provinces. Now that the Japanese are increasingly ambitious to seize Chinese silk, your association did not find a way to resist it, but because of this year's poor silkworm cocoon harvest, fearing that the silk factories in Shanghai would not have enough supply, it initiated the purchase of Japanese cocoons and requested a reduction in import taxes to reduce the cost of shipping to China so that silk factories could purchase them. Your association's plan for the silk factories is indeed good, but because our country's silkworm breeding methods mostly adhere to old habits and have not been fully improved, the quality of the cocoons and silk reeling are difficult to compete with Japanese cocoons. If Japanese cocoons continue to be shipped in according to established cases, not only will the silkworm factories in the inland areas face failure, but also the Chinese cocoons will be infringed upon by Japanese cocoons, and the beauty and profit of silkworm farming will decline. This is tantamount to fueling the Japanese desire to seize Chinese silk. It is nominally to help silk factories in Shanghai, but it is no different from driving the silk cocoons of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui provinces to the brink of extinction. It is found that a large number of inland silk cocoons have been transported to Shanghai and stored in warehouses awaiting sale this year. The reason why silk factories have recently stopped working is due to the sluggish sales of foreign silk and the accumulation of inventory. It is not due to a lack of raw materials. To seek the future development of Chinese silk and the current relief, the fundamental solution is to reduce the export tax on raw silk and various surcharges on dry cocoons. The symptomatic solution is to temporarily exempt all taxes and fees related to Chinese silk, add a period and limit on the amount, so that tax revenue and commerce are not hindered. If your association can unite the power of silk cocoon merchants from the three provinces to achieve the goal of exemption or reduction, the accumulated difficulties of silk cocoons may have a day of recovery. If you only plead for Japanese merchants, your plan will be unwise. No wonder the silkworm industry in the inland areas has complained. Our association has already submitted the previous opinions to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for adoption. If your association agrees, we hope that you will advocate for it together.

Telegram to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce: Respectfully, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce of the National Government, according to a telegram from the Jiaxing Silk Cocoon Association stating that the import of Japanese dry cocoons will lead to the demise of the Chinese silk cocoon industry, which is of great importance to national taxes and commerce. The telegram requests a swift method of resistance, which is a common feeling. It was submitted to the board of directors meeting on September 13 for discussion. Everyone agreed that the import of foreign raw materials is indeed a good sign for our country's industry, but the import of raw materials as Japanese dry cocoons is of great importance to the future of our country's silkworm industry. If Japanese cocoons continue to come in, not only will the silkworm factories in the inland areas fail, but also because our country's silkworm breeding methods have not been fully improved, they may decline due to the infringement of Japanese cocoons. The General Association of Silk Cocoons of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui provinces holds the key to the silk cocoons of the three provinces. Because of this year's poor harvest, fearing that the silk factories in Shanghai would not have enough supply, they purchased Japanese cocoons and requested a reduction in import taxes, which is tantamount to fueling the Japanese desire to seize Chinese silk. It is nominally to help silk factories in Shanghai, but it is no different from driving the silk cocoons of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui provinces to the brink of extinction. It is found that there are still quite a few leftover cocoons from inland areas transported to Shanghai and stored in warehouses awaiting sale this year. The reason why silk factories have recently stopped working is due to the sluggish sales of foreign silk and the accumulation of inventory. It is not due to a lack of raw materials. Our association advocates that to seek the future development of Chinese silk and the current relief, the fundamental solution is to reduce the export tax on raw silk and various surcharges on dry cocoons. The symptomatic solution is to temporarily exempt all taxes and fees, but restrictions on the period and amount must be added to avoid hindering tax revenue. Our association believes that silk cocoons are our country's inherent beauty, which is related to national tax revenue and people's livelihoods. We sincerely ask the ministry to review and adopt our views, and to cancel the reduction of import taxes on Japanese cocoons in order to comply with the situation. Our association is very grateful, and the nation is grateful. The Zhejiang General Chamber of Commerce kowtows.

Zhejiang Navigation Administration Bureau Expands Inland River Shipping

The Navigation Administration Bureau of the Construction Department of Zhejiang Province has leased all of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's inland river ships to develop Zhejiang's shipping industry, which has been reported in this newspaper. Recently, General Manager Chen Shuntong, Associate Manager Sheng Nian, Shanghai Manager Zhang Shusheng, and others have agreed on further expansion measures. The latest news is divided as follows:

Opening Up Upstream Routes: The upper reaches of the Qiantang River in Zhejiang, such as Yuhang, Fuyang, Jinhua, Jianxi, etc., are prosperous areas for Zhejiang's trade, but there are no scheduled ships, which hinders the development of transportation and commerce. The bureau, under the main purpose of the Construction Department, is planning to add upstream ships. General Manager Chen Shuntong and Zhang Shusheng have decided to divide the upper reaches of the Qiantang River into six routes. It is planned to open two or three routes first so that passengers and goods from Yuhang and other places can be connected to Shanghai. Chen Shuntong went to Hangzhou yesterday to discuss the implementation plan with the Construction Department.

Assigning Existing Routes: After the bureau took over, it has now allocated and operated all routes. They are specifically listed as follows: (1) Shanghai-Hangzhou route: Hengren and Lixiang ships. (2) Shanghai-Huzhou route: Hengji and Liyuan ships. (3) Shanghai-Suzhou route: He'an and Gonglong ships. (4) Suzhou-Hangzhou route: Lihang, Lichuan, and Hengsheng ships. (5) Zhenjiang route: Junfa, Hengtong, and Hekuan ships. (6) Xicheng route: Taichang and Yuren ships. (7) Xili route: Jianyuan ship. (8) Jiahu route: Dehe ship. (9) Changli route: Jianyuan ship. (10) Changqing route: Ruishun ship. (11) Sudang route: Xiangfu ship. (12) Xunjia route: Feilong ship. (13) Puchang route: Feima ship. In addition, Yonggu is assigned to Yangxiang, Xin'an is assigned to Pingxia, Junfeng is sailing to Dutou Xueli is sailing to Xiashi, and Hongan is rented out. Hengfeng is under repair.

Eliminating Bad Habits in Various Ports: The bureau adopts the principle of integrity and focuses on facilitating merchants in the water transport fees of various ports. It breaks all bad habits such as rebates and strictly orders branch bureaus in various ports to collect ship tickets at fixed prices, eliminating the long-standing evil of foreign water peeling. For example, violations will be severely punished. The practice of adding water to ticket sales is the worst long-standing habit of inland river ships, which is difficult to break. Now the bureau has strictly eliminated this malpractice, so that travelers can avoid the pain of unexpected losses. Shanghai Bureau Director Zhang Shusheng is especially strict and upright in handling affairs. No matter how busy the incoming and outgoing documents are, they are not allowed to be delayed for a moment and must be handled on the same day. Therefore, the bureau is full of vitality and the future is very optimistic. The total annual business of the bureau is 400,000 yuan. After the opening of the new route in Zhejiang and the completion of intermodal transport, it is expected to increase revenue.

Guangji Ship Released and Returned to Shanghai

Two Compradors Released and Returned to Shanghai

Ships Operate on Regular Schedule

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Guangji ship was detained in Wenzhou because the crew member Liu Fulai was an escapee. Yesterday, the ship had returned to Shanghai. According to the crew, when the Guangji arrived in Wenzhou, the 19th Army learned that the watchman Liu Fulai was a member of the Communist Party, so they sent more than 70 soldiers to the ship to arrest Liu. Liu had gone ashore after the ship arrived at the dock, so the soldiers came and Liu had left the ship. The soldiers searched the ship for a long time. Because they did not find Liu Fulai, they detained the two compradors, Wang Shoukang, to the headquarters. They learned that the crew was completely unaware of Liu's joining the party and had no relationship with colleagues in the bureau. Therefore, they ordered the Guangji crew to provide a guarantee and released Wang Shoukang. Wang was detained at the headquarters of the 19th Army for a day and returned to Shanghai on the original Guangji ship yesterday. According to the Communist Party roster seized by the 19th Army, Liu Fulai was responsible for transmitting the party's messages and correspondence between Shanghai and Wenzhou, and his responsibilities were very important. Once he is caught, he will be able to extract information about the Communist Party's organizations and actions in Shanghai and other places. The 19th Army believed that this matter had nothing to do with the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and the Guangji ship, so they did not delay and released the ship, ordering it to unload cargo as usual, so it was not delayed. It has now returned to Shanghai. Liu is still at large in Wenzhou and is now under strict arrest.

Land Bureau Urges the Collection of Land Practice Certificates

Failure to Collect within the Deadline Will Be Subject to Punishment

Article 14 of the Shanghai Municipal Regulations on the Issuance of Land Practice Certificates stipulates that after the expiration of one year from the date of public announcement of the issuance of land certificates for surveyed land, those who have not collected them must be notified by the Land Bureau to collect them. If they still delay in collecting them after six months, the Land Bureau will report to the Municipal Government for punishment. Now, the period for issuing land certificates for the 25th Bao 4th Tu has expired for one year, and there are still a few owners who have not collected them. The Land Bureau has ordered the local security of the Tu to notify the owners to collect them as soon as possible. If they do not collect them after six months, they will be reported to the Municipal Government for punishment in accordance with the regulations.

Cotton Crop Failure in Various Zhai Towns West of Shanghai

Ninth District, Fourteenth Precinct Submits Request for Tax Reduction

Seventy to eighty percent of the farmers in the various Zhai towns west of Shanghai rely on cotton planting for their livelihood. Since the beginning of summer this year, the rainfall has been irregular, and the cotton harvest is only about ten catties per mu. The farmers throughout the towns are worried and gloomy because they have no hope for the autumn harvest. The Fourteenth Precinct of the Ninth District of the city has submitted a report on the drought in the towns to higher authorities, requesting that it be forwarded to the municipal government to reduce or exempt taxes. The original report is recorded as follows:

Respectfully submitted by the undersigned precinct, since the beginning of summer in the Zhai towns, the rainfall has been irregular, and the temperature has been uneven. As a result, the cotton in the fields has flowered but not fruited, and the yield per mu is mostly only a dozen catties. It is estimated that the value per mu is only a little over one yuan. In the worst cases, this amount is not enough to provide warmth and food for a family of several people. Those in the villages who plant cotton account for seventy to eighty percent of the population. The autumn harvest is hopeless, and a local famine has already occurred. It is foreseeable that people's livelihoods will be difficult in the future. Therefore, we are especially listing the grievances and earnestly requesting that you forward them to the superior party department and consult with the Shanghai Municipal Government and the Jiading and Qingpu County Governments to quickly dispatch special commissioners to the countryside to investigate the disaster-stricken areas and grant them tax reductions and exemptions, thereby prioritizing the people's livelihood.

Agricultural Products to Be Inspected

Procedures for Customs Declaration of Exports and Transshipments

Registration to Begin with Grains and Rice, Followed by Wheat and Flour

The Shanghai Agricultural Products Inspection Institute recently submitted a report to the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining, requesting that it be forwarded to the Executive Yuan to instruct the Ministry of Finance to issue a notice to the customs to assist and allocate funds for implementation. It also proposed to start with grain and rice inspection and registration. The original report stated that all those who trade, import, export, and transship food should first report to the local inspection and registration authorities for inspection and registration. Only after the stamp of the seal is affixed can customs be declared. In fact, unless this is done, grain merchants cannot be made to comply uniformly. However, if this method is implemented without the assistance of the customs, it is feared that unscrupulous merchants will regard it as a mere formality and evade smuggling, and the inspection authorities will not be able to impose sanctions, resulting in omissions. This would defeat the central government's plan to statistically analyze food and regulate people's food supply. This kind of problem is not unique to Shanghai; it is also difficult to avoid at ports in various places. Therefore, when the institute starts, it will notify all grain merchants to comply. In addition, it is proposed that your ministry forward the report to the Executive Yuan to instruct the Ministry of Finance to notify the customs to assist. In the future, when encountering customs declarations for importing, exporting, and transshipping food, customs officials should order the merchants to first send the customs declaration, bill of lading, permit, and other related documents to the food inspection and registration authorities in the respective areas to affix the seal before allowing customs declaration and release to prevent smuggling. Furthermore, the institute previously requested the addition of a special class for inspection and registration of food and the compilation of a minimum budget for temporary and recurring expenses for the class, which was sent to your ministry to be forwarded to the Executive Yuan for approval to add the special class and to instruct the Ministry of Finance to allocate funds. Now that the class has been prepared, the implementation of inspection and registration is imminent. Please quickly present the matter to the Executive Yuan to instruct the Ministry of Finance to reallocate the funds urgently. Furthermore, Article 4 of the regulations stipulates that food inspection and registration should be implemented in stages according to procedures. The intention is that the needs of the people's food supply should vary from place to place. Rice is the main staple in the south, and the institute should start with rice protection. Once the scale is gradually established, wheat flour and other foods can be added in order. The Ministry of Agriculture and Mining has submitted a report to the Executive Yuan, and the Executive Yuan has ordered the Ministry of Finance to instruct the customs to assist in the inspection and registration matters. The addition of a special class and budget has also been approved by the Executive Yuan. The registration of grains and rice first has also been ordered and approved by the Ministry of Agriculture.

Red Cross Revises Constitution Committee

Continued Closed Session

The Chinese Red Cross Society's Constitution Revision Committee held its twelfth meeting at 2 p.m. on September 17th. The committee members present were Li Zhenbang, Wen Lanting, Jiang Daqiu, Wu Jiasan, Ye Zhisheng, Wang Peiyuan, Wang Xiaolai, Liu Hongsheng, Yang Ke, Xue Shaoting, Dong Xinqin, Xu Xichun, and Hong Yanbin. Wen Lanting chaired the meeting, and Wei Ruifeng recorded the proceedings. After customary greetings, the minutes of the previous meeting were read and signed by the chairman.

(1) The chairman reported that today would be the second reading of the Executive Committee Regulations and Branch Office Guidelines, starting with the Executive Committee Regulations.

(1) Fang Xiqi suggested that clauses thirteen, fourteen, fifteen, and sixteen should be revised, and the order should be changed. Wu Jiasan seconded the motion. By common agreement, clause six was changed to clause thirteen, and its text was changed to: "In order to handle its affairs, the society shall establish six departments: Documentation, Economic Affairs, Disaster Relief, Medical Affairs, Youth Affairs, and Promotion. Each department shall have a director elected by the Executive Committee to handle all affairs of the society. The Branch Office Guidelines and detailed rules of procedure shall be formulated separately." Clause fourteen remained unchanged, and its text was changed to: "The society shall appoint a general manager to handle daily affairs under the supervision of the society, who shall be appointed by the Executive Committee." Clause fifteen remained unchanged, and its text was changed to: "The general manager may attend committee meetings to present opinions." Clause thirteen was changed to clause sixteen, and its text was changed to: "The society shall appoint a secretary to record meeting minutes, organize proposals, and draft correspondence, who shall be appointed by the Executive Committee."

(1) Li Zhenbang suggested that the phrase "the term of office for consultants shall be limited to the term of the society" in clause seventeen could be deleted, and the phrase "may invite them to attend meetings" should be changed to "may attend meetings to present opinions."

(1) The chairman suggested that the legal consultant in clause eighteen could be merged into clause seventeen, and the society should invite an accountant to audit the society's accounts. Wu Jiasan suggested that the text of clause eighteen could be changed to: "The society shall hire an accountant to audit all income and expenses of the society. The selection of the person and the amount of public funds must be approved by the standing council and appointed by the chairman. The term of office is one year and may be renewed."

(1) Wang Peiyuan suggested that clause nineteen should also be revised. By common agreement: "These regulations shall take effect upon passage by the standing council. Amendments to these regulations may be submitted by the Executive Committee with the consent of the standing committee."

(1) The chairman reported that the second reading of the Executive Committee Regulations had been completed and that the second reading of the Executive Committee Branch Office Guidelines would now continue.

(1) Wang Peiyuan suggested that the phrase "and establish temporary wounded soldier hospitals and burial teams" should be added to item five of clause six. In addition, item two of clause seven should be changed to "Launching a major campaign to recruit youth members" and adding items: "Education on the moral, intellectual, and physical development of youth" in item seven and "Interactions between youth of Red Cross societies in various countries" in item eight.

(1) The chairman suggested that the provision on dividing the work of ten bureaus should be postponed and could be deleted. Wang Peiyuan seconded the motion.

(1) The chairman reported that the second readings of the Executive Committee Regulations and Branch Office Guidelines had been completed and that the rules of procedure would be read for the first time tomorrow. The meeting adjourned at 5 p.m.

Lawyers Association Joint Meeting of Directors and Supervisors

Sixty-Third Meeting

The Shanghai Lawyers Association convened its sixty-third joint meeting of directors and supervisors at 6 p.m. yesterday. Chairman Liu Zuwang conducted the meeting with customary greetings and presented the following proposals:

(1) A case in which the Jiangsu High Court requested the second reissuance of lawyer certificates with attached photos has been completed, and the certificates are enclosed for distribution. It was resolved that the certificates would be distributed to the members for collection at the members' general meeting on the 21st of this month.

(2) Committee member Yu Jingluo proposed that the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau's announcement, issued by order of the Municipal Government, to strictly crack down on rent arrears, raises doubts about the infringement of judicial power. An emergency discussion was held on a plan to protest and prevent this. (The full text is recorded below.) The committee members considered this matter to be important and resolved to send a letter to the Municipal Government inquiring about the specific methods and boundaries of cracking down on rent arrears and whether it involves judicial power. At the same time, they will submit a request to the Ministry of Judicial Administration to instruct the courts to vigorously implement provisional execution and other preservation measures for rent arrears cases and to pay attention to the Police Bureau's announcement to prevent the infringement of judicial power.

(3) Applications for membership from lawyers Xu Xiangshu and Wang Jing and others were approved.

(4) A letter from member Li Shirui regarding the extension of a loan was resolved to be answered, requesting that it be repaid by the end of this year.

(5) Member Shen Xiaoxiang proposed that the autumn general meeting should elect a presidium of twelve or fifteen people. It was resolved that, according to Article 18 of the association's rules, this case is not established, and a letter of response should be sent to the original proposer for their information.

(6) The presidium for this year's autumn general meeting should be determined quickly. It was resolved to elect committee members Liu Zuwang, Jiang Yiping, and Tan Yigong as the presidium.

(7) Member Shen Xiaoxiang proposed that the judicial and legislative branches should abolish the old practice of "father's debts are inherited by the son." It was resolved to answer the case with a letter.

The proposal of committee member Yu Jingluo is recorded below:

Regarding the proposal, on the 14th of this month, newspapers reported a notice from the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau (政字第25號) regarding the crackdown on rent arrears, stating that "this matter of rent arrears has recently been ordered by the Municipal Government to be cracked down on, and it should be handled conscientiously in accordance with one's duties. If any cases of arbitrary rent arrears are found in the future, the landlords should report them immediately, and they will be strictly cracked down on without any leniency. It is hoped that all residents in the area will comply." The specific methods of "strict crackdown" are not explicitly stated, but it can be inferred that they would include urging payment, summoning for questioning, detention, or sealing and eviction. All of these measures are the inherent functions of the court and should not be usurped by the Police Bureau. The Police Bureau's announcement states that it was ordered by the Municipal Government to crack down on rent arrears, but it is not known what legal basis there is for this. It is true that landlords in Shanghai suffer from the pain of rent arrears, but there is no absolute lack of remedies in litigation law. If the judicial authorities vigorously implement provisional execution and other preservation procedures, it would be sufficient to reduce delays and prevent escapes. To entrust the power of cracking down to the police for arbitrary disposition is to seek convenience for a small number of landlords at the expense of the entire judicial power, exposing our shortcomings to foreign observers in Shanghai. The impact of this cannot be overstated. The association seems unable to remain silent on this important issue. Therefore, it is proposed that an emergency meeting should be convened to discuss a concrete plan to protest and prevent this in order to maintain legal rights.
